from enum import Enum
from sqlalchemy import Enum as PgEnum, DateTime
from datetime import datetime

class OrderStatus(str, Enum):
    CREATED = "created"
    PAID = "paid"
    ASSIGNED = "assigned"
    IN_PROGRESS = "in_progress"
    COMPLETED = "completed"
    CANCELLED = "cancelled"

class OrderModel(Base):
    __tablename__ = "orders"
    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer)
    service_type = Column(String)
    status = Column(PgEnum(OrderStatus), default=OrderStatus.CREATED)
    created_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow)

class Order(BaseModel):
    id: int
    service_type: str
    status: OrderStatus
    created_at: datetime

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True

@app.post("/orders", response_model=Order)
def create_order(service_type: str, db: Session = Depends(get_db), user: UserModel = Depends(get_current_user)):
    order = OrderModel(user_id=user.id, service_type=service_type)
    db.add(order)
    db.commit()
    db.refresh(order)
    notify(user.email, f"Order {order.id} created")
    return order

@app.post("/orders/{order_id}/status")
def update_order_status(order_id: int, status: OrderStatus, db: Session = Depends(get_db)):
    order = db.query(OrderModel).get(order_id)
    if not order:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Order not found")
    order.status = status
    db.commit()
    notify("admin", f"Order {order.id} status updated to {status}")
    return {"status": order.status}

@app.get("/orders", response_model=List[Order])
def list_orders(db: Session = Depends(get_db), user: UserModel = Depends(get_current_user)):
    return db.query(OrderModel).filter(OrderModel.user_id == user.id).all()

See my thinking
Here’s a complete minimal but working example: FastAPI backend + simple HTML/JS frontend in one project.

I’ll give you:

Project structure

Backend (FastAPI + SQLAlchemy + SQLite)

Frontend (single-page HTML + JS calling the APIs)

How to run

You can extend it later (auth, real DB, styling, etc.).

1. Project structure

├─ backend/
│  ├─ main.py

2. Backend code
backend/database.py
python


Copy
from sqlalchemy import create_engine
from sqlalchemy.orm import sessionmaker, declarative_base

SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URL = "sqlite:///./superapp.db"

engine = create_engine(
    SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URL, connect_args={"check_same_thread": False}
)

SessionLocal = sessionmaker(autocommit=False, autoflush=False, bind=engine)

Base = declarative_base()


def get_db():
    db = SessionLocal()
    try:
        yield db
    finally:
        db.close()
backend/models.py
python


Copy
from sqlalchemy import Column, Integer, String, Enum as PgEnum, DateTime, ForeignKey
from sqlalchemy.orm import relationship
from datetime import datetime
from enum import Enum

from .database import Base


class OrderStatus(str, Enum):
    CREATED = "created"
    PAID = "paid"
    ASSIGNED = "assigned"
    IN_PROGRESS = "in_progress"
    COMPLETED = "completed"
    CANCELLED = "cancelled"


class UserModel(Base):
    __tablename__ = "users"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    email = Column(String, unique=True, index=True)
    role = Column(String, default="user")

    orders = relationship("OrderModel", back_populates="user")


class RestaurantModel(Base):
    __tablename__ = "restaurants"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    name = Column(String, index=True)
    cuisine = Column(String)
    location = Column(String)


class ChargerModel(Base):
    __tablename__ = "chargers"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    name = Column(String)
    location = Column(String)
    status = Column(String, default="available")


class OrderModel(Base):
    __tablename__ = "orders"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer, ForeignKey("users.id"))
    service_type = Column(String)
    status = Column(PgEnum(OrderStatus), default=OrderStatus.CREATED)
    created_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow)

    user = relationship("UserModel", back_populates="orders")
backend/schemas.py
python


Copy
from pydantic import BaseModel
from datetime import datetime
from enum import Enum
from typing import List


class OrderStatus(str, Enum):
    CREATED = "created"
    PAID = "paid"
    ASSIGNED = "assigned"
    IN_PROGRESS = "in_progress"
    COMPLETED = "completed"
    CANCELLED = "cancelled"


# --- Restaurants ---

class Restaurant(BaseModel):
    id: int
    name: str
    cuisine: str
    location: str

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True


# --- EV chargers ---

class Charger(BaseModel):
    id: int
    name: str
    location: str
    status: str

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True


# --- Ride hailing ---

class RideRequest(BaseModel):
    pickup: str
    dropoff: str
    ride_type: str


# --- Parcel delivery ---

class ParcelRequest(BaseModel):
    sender: str
    receiver: str
    size: str


# --- Orders ---

class Order(BaseModel):
    id: int
    service_type: str
    status: OrderStatus
    created_at: datetime

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True


# --- Users ---

class User(BaseModel):
    id: int
    email: str
    role: str

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True
backend/deps.py
Simple fake auth using a header X-User-Email (or default user).

python


Copy
from fastapi import Depends, Header, HTTPException
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session

from .database import get_db
from . import models


def get_current_user(
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    x_user_email: str | None = Header(default=None),
):
    # Very simple auth: get or create user by email header
    email = x_user_email or "user@example.com"

    user = db.query(models.UserModel).filter(models.UserModel.email == email).first()
    if not user:
        user = models.UserModel(email=email, role="user")
        db.add(user)
        db.commit()
        db.refresh(user)
    return user


def get_admin_user(
    current_user: models.UserModel = Depends(get_current_user),
):
    if current_user.role != "admin":
        raise HTTPException(status_code=403, detail="Admin only")
    return current_user
backend/main.py
python


Copy
from fastapi import FastAPI, Depends, HTTPException
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware
from fastapi.staticfiles import StaticFiles
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from typing import List

from .database import Base, engine, get_db
from . import models, schemas
from .deps import get_current_user, get_admin_user


# Create tables
Base.metadata.create_all(bind=engine)

app = FastAPI(title="Super App")


# CORS (allow frontend HTML opened from file or localhost)
app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=["*"],
    allow_methods=["*"],
    allow_headers=["*"],
)


# Optional: serve frontend if you copy index.html into ./backend/static
# app.mount("/", StaticFiles(directory="static", html=True), name="static")


# --- Utility notification ---

def notify(target: str, message: str):
    print(f"[NOTIFY] {target}: {message}")


# --- Food delivery ---

@app.get("/restaurants", response_model=List[schemas.Restaurant])
def list_restaurants(db: Session = Depends(get_db)):
    return db.query(models.RestaurantModel).all()


# --- Ride hailing ---

@app.post("/rides/request")
def request_ride(
    data: schemas.RideRequest,
    user: models.UserModel = Depends(get_current_user),
):
    notify(user.email, f"Ride requested from {data.pickup} to {data.dropoff}")
    return {"status": "requested", "ride": data, "user": user.email}


# --- Parcel delivery ---

@app.post("/parcels")
def create_parcel(
    data: schemas.ParcelRequest,
    user: models.UserModel = Depends(get_current_user),
):
    notify(user.email, f"Parcel created from {data.sender} to {data.receiver}")
    return {"status": "created", "parcel": data, "user": user.email}


# --- Orders ---

@app.post("/orders", response_model=schemas.Order)
def create_order(
    service_type: str,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    user: models.UserModel = Depends(get_current_user),
):
    order = models.OrderModel(user_id=user.id, service_type=service_type)
    db.add(order)
    db.commit()
    db.refresh(order)
    notify(user.email, f"Order {order.id} created")
    return order


@app.post("/orders/{order_id}/status")
def update_order_status(
    order_id: int,
    status: schemas.OrderStatus,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
):
    order = db.query(models.OrderModel).get(order_id)
    if not order:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Order not found")
    order.status = status
    db.commit()
    notify("admin", f"Order {order.id} status updated to {status}")
    return {"status": order.status}


@app.get("/orders", response_model=List[schemas.Order])
def list_orders(
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    user: models.UserModel = Depends(get_current_user),
):
    return db.query(models.OrderModel).filter(models.OrderModel.user_id == user.id).all()


# --- EV charging ---

@app.get("/chargers", response_model=List[schemas.Charger])
def list_chargers(db: Session = Depends(get_db)):
    return db.query(models.ChargerModel).all()


# --- Admin ---

@app.get("/admin/users", response_model=List[schemas.User])
def admin_users(
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    admin: models.UserModel = Depends(get_admin_user),
):
    return db.query(models.UserModel).all()


# --- Health ---

@app.get("/health")
def health():
    return {"status": "ok"}
3. Frontend (single page)
frontend/index.html
This uses plain HTML + JS (no build tools). It calls the backend at http://localhost:8000.

html


Copy
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
  <meta charset="UTF-8" />
  <title>Super App Demo</title>
  <style>
    body { font-family: Arial, sans-serif; margin: 20px; }
    nav button { margin-right: 10px; }
    .section { display: none; margin-top: 20px; }
    .section.active { display: block; }
    pre { background: #f5f5f5; padding: 10px; }
    input, select, button { margin: 5px 0; display: block; }
  </style>
</head>
<body>
  <h1>Super App Demo</h1>

  <label>
    X-User-Email (for fake auth):
    <input id="userEmail" type="email" placeholder="user@example.com" />
  </label>

  <nav>
    <button onclick="showSection('food')">Food Delivery</button>
    <button onclick="showSection('ride')">Ride Hailing</button>
    <button onclick="showSection('parcel')">Parcel Delivery</button>
    <button onclick="showSection('orders')">Orders</button>
    <button onclick="showSection('charging')">EV Charging</button>
    <button onclick="showSection('admin')">Admin</button>
  </nav>

  <!-- Food Delivery -->
  <div id="section-food" class="section active">
    <h2>Food Delivery - Restaurants</h2>
    <button onclick="fetchRestaurants()">Load Restaurants</button>
    <pre id="restaurantsOutput"></pre>
  </div>

  <!-- Ride Hailing -->
  <div id="section-ride" class="section">
    <h2>Ride Hailing - Request Ride</h2>
    <label>Pickup: <input id="ridePickup" /></label>
    <label>Dropoff: <input id="rideDropoff" /></label>
    <label>
      Ride Type:
      <select id="rideType">
        <option value="standard">Standard</option>
        <option value="motorbike">Motorbike</option>
        <option value="premium">Premium</option>
      </select>
    </label>
    <button onclick="requestRide()">Request Ride</button>
    <pre id="rideOutput"></pre>
  </div>

  <!-- Parcel Delivery -->
  <div id="section-parcel" class="section">
    <h2>Parcel Delivery - Create Parcel</h2>
    <label>Sender: <input id="parcelSender" /></label>
    <label>Receiver: <input id="parcelReceiver" /></label>
    <label>
      Size:
      <select id="parcelSize">
        <option value="small">Small</option>
        <option value="medium">Medium</option>
        <option value="large">Large</option>
      </select>
    </label>
    <button onclick="createParcel()">Create Parcel</button>
    <pre id="parcelOutput"></pre>
  </div>

  <!-- Orders -->
  <div id="section-orders" class="section">
    <h2>Orders</h2>
    <h3>Create Order</h3>
    <label>
      Service Type:
      <select id="orderServiceType">
        <option value="food_delivery">Food Delivery</option>
        <option value="ride_hailing">Ride Hailing</option>
        <option value="parcel_delivery">Parcel Delivery</option>
        <option value="ev_charging">EV Charging</option>
      </select>
    </label>
    <button onclick="createOrder()">Create Order</button>

    <h3>My Orders</h3>
    <button onclick="fetchOrders()">Load My Orders</button>
    <pre id="ordersOutput"></pre>
  </div>

  <!-- EV Charging -->
  <div id="section-charging" class="section">
    <h2>EV Charging - Chargers</h2>
    <button onclick="fetchChargers()">Load Chargers</button>
    <pre id="chargersOutput"></pre>
  </div>

  <!-- Admin -->
  <div id="section-admin" class="section">
    <h2>Admin - Users</h2>
    <p>To act as admin, set email to something like admin@example.com and update it manually in DB (role='admin').</p>
    <button onclick="fetchUsers()">Load Users</button>
    <pre id="usersOutput"></pre>
  </div>

  <script>
    const BASE_URL = "http://localhost:8000";

    function getHeaders() {
      const email = document.getElementById("userEmail").value || "user@example.com";
      return {
        "Content-Type": "application/json",
        "X-User-Email": email
      };
    }

    function showSection(name) {
      document.querySelectorAll(".section").forEach(sec => sec.classList.remove("active"));
      document.getElementById("section-" + name).classList.add("active");
    }

    // --- Food Delivery ---

    async function fetchRestaurants() {
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/restaurants`, { headers: getHeaders() });
      const data = await res.json();
      document.getElementById("restaurantsOutput").textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
    }

    // --- Ride Hailing ---

    async function requestRide() {
      const body = {
        pickup: document.getElementById("ridePickup").value,
        dropoff: document.getElementById("rideDropoff").value,
        ride_type: document.getElementById("rideType").value
      };
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/rides/request`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: getHeaders(),
        body: JSON.stringify(body)
      });
      const data = await res.json();
      document.getElementById("rideOutput").textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
    }

    // --- Parcel Delivery ---

    async function createParcel() {
      const body = {
        sender: document.getElementById("parcelSender").value,
        receiver: document.getElementById("parcelReceiver").value,
        size: document.getElementById("parcelSize").value
      };
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/parcels`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: getHeaders(),
        body: JSON.stringify(body)
      });
      const data = await res.json();
      document.getElementById("parcelOutput").textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
    }

    // --- Orders ---

    async function createOrder() {
      const serviceType = document.getElementById("orderServiceType").value;
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/orders?service_type=${encodeURIComponent(serviceType)}`, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: getHeaders()
      });
      const data = await res.json();
      fetchOrders();
    }

    async function fetchOrders() {
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/orders`, {
        headers: getHeaders()
      });
      const data = await res.json();
      document.getElementById("ordersOutput").textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
    }

    // --- EV Charging ---

    async function fetchChargers() {
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/chargers`, { headers: getHeaders() });
      const data = await res.json();
      document.getElementById("chargersOutput").textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
    }

    // --- Admin ---

    async function fetchUsers() {
      const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}/admin/users`, { headers: getHeaders() });
      const data = await res.json();
      document.getElementById("usersOutput").textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
    }
  </script>
</body>
</html>
4. Setup and run
From the superapp root:

Create and activate virtualenv (optional but recommended).

Install backend deps:

bash


Copy
cd backend
pip install fastapi uvicorn sqlalchemy pydantic "pydantic[email]" python-multipart
(Optional) seed some data (restaurants, chargers) using a quick Python script or via FastAPI docs (http://localhost:8000/docs) once running.

Start backend:

bash


Copy
uvicorn backend.main:app --reload
Open the frontend:

Easiest: open frontend/index.html directly in your browser, or

Serve it with a simple server:

bash


Copy
cd frontend
python -m http.server 5500
Then open http://localhost:5500 in your browser.

If you want, next step we can:

Add JWT auth instead of the fake header

Add proper create endpoints for restaurants/chargers

Replace the plain HTML with a React or Next.js frontend consuming the same APIs.

Replace the plain HTML with a React or Next.js frontend consuming the same APIs.
Copilot said
Absolutely — let’s level this up. Since you’re building a super‑app with multiple modules (rides, parcels, food, EV charging, orders, admin), Next.js is the perfect fit. It gives you routing, API integration, SSR/ISR if you ever need it, and a clean developer experience.

Below is a complete working Next.js frontend that consumes your FastAPI backend exactly as‑is.

I’ll give you:

✅ Project structure
✅ Pages for each module
✅ API helper for calling FastAPI
✅ Components for forms & lists
✅ Instructions to run
Everything is modular so you can expand it into a full super‑app UI later.

🧩 2. API Client (centralized)
components/ApiClient.js
javascript


Copy
const BASE_URL = "http://localhost:8000";

export async function api(path, method = "GET", body = null, email = null) {
  const headers = {
    "Content-Type": "application/json",
    "X-User-Email": email || "user@example.com",
  };

  const res = await fetch(`${BASE_URL}${path}`, {
    method,
    headers,
    body: body ? JSON.stringify(body) : null,
  });

  return res.json();
}

🍽️ 5. Restaurants Page
pages/restaurants.js
javascript


Copy
import { useState } from "react";
import Layout from "../components/Layout";
import { api } from "../components/ApiClient";

export default function Restaurants() {
  const [data, setData] = useState([]);

  async function load() {
    setData(await api("/restaurants"));
  }

  return (
    <Layout>
      <h2>Restaurants</h2>
      <button onClick={load}>Load Restaurants</button>
      <pre>{JSON.stringify(data, null, 2)}</pre>
    </Layout>
  );
}
🚕 6. Ride Request Page
pages/ride.js
javascript


Copy
import { useState } from "react";
import Layout from "../components/Layout";
import { api } from "../components/ApiClient";

export default function Ride() {
  const [pickup, setPickup] = useState("");
  const [dropoff, setDropoff] = useState("");
  const [rideType, setRideType] = useState("standard");
  const [result, setResult] = useState(null);

  async function requestRide() {
    const res = await api("/rides/request", "POST", {
      pickup,
      dropoff,
      ride_type: rideType,
    });
    setResult(res);
  }

  return (
    <Layout>
      <h2>Request Ride</h2>

      <input placeholder="Pickup" onChange={(e) => setPickup(e.target.value)} />
      <input placeholder="Dropoff" onChange={(e) => setDropoff(e.target.value)} />

      <select onChange={(e) => setRideType(e.target.value)}>
        <option value="standard">Standard</option>
        <option value="motorbike">Motorbike</option>
        <option value="premium">Premium</option>
      </select>

      <button onClick={requestRide}>Request Ride</button>

      <pre>{JSON.stringify(result, null, 2)}</pre>
    </Layout>
  );
}
📦 7. Parcel Page
pages/parcel.js
javascript


Copy
import { useState } from "react";
import Layout from "../components/Layout";
import { api } from "../components/ApiClient";

export default function Parcel() {
  const [sender, setSender] = useState("");
  const [receiver, setReceiver] = useState("");
  const [size, setSize] = useState("small");
  const [result, setResult] = useState(null);

  async function createParcel() {
    const res = await api("/parcels", "POST", {
      sender,
      receiver,
      size,
    });
    setResult(res);
  }

  return (
    <Layout>
      <h2>Create Parcel</h2>

      <input placeholder="Sender" onChange={(e) => setSender(e.target.value)} />
      <input placeholder="Receiver" onChange={(e) => setReceiver(e.target.value)} />

      <select onChange={(e) => setSize(e.target.value)}>
        <option value="small">Small</option>
        <option value="medium">Medium</option>
        <option value="large">Large</option>
      </select>

      <button onClick={createParcel}>Create Parcel</button>

      <pre>{JSON.stringify(result, null, 2)}</pre>
    </Layout>
  );
}
📜 8. Orders Page

Copy
import { useState } from "react";
import Layout from "../components/Layout";
import { api } from "../components/ApiClient";

export default function Orders() {
  const [orders, setOrders] = useState([]);

  async function loadOrders() {
    setOrders(await api("/orders"));
  }

  async function createOrder() {
    const serviceType = prompt("Enter service type (food_delivery, ride_hailing, parcel_delivery, ev_charging)");
    await api(`/orders?service_type=${serviceType}`, "POST");
    loadOrders();
  }

  return (
    <Layout>
      <h2>Orders</h2>

      <button onClick={createOrder}>Create Order</button>
      <button onClick={loadOrders}>Load My Orders</button>

      <pre>{JSON.stringify(orders, null, 2)}</pre>
    </Layout>
  );
}

Absolutely, Sebastian — now that your backend is running cleanly, let’s make your life easier by creating one PowerShell script that starts BOTH the FastAPI backend and the Next.js frontend automatically.

Below is a clean, production‑ready script.

🚀 PowerShell Script: start-superapp.ps1
Copy this into a file named:

Code


Copy
start-superapp.ps1
Place it inside your Superapp root folder (the folder that contains both backend and superapp-frontend).

# ================================
# SuperApp Startup Script
# Starts FastAPI backend + Next.js frontend
# ================================

Write-Host "Starting SuperApp..." -ForegroundColor Cyan

# --- Step 1: Start FastAPI backend ---
Write-Host "`n[1/2] Starting FastAPI backend..." -ForegroundColor Yellow

Start-Process powershell -ArgumentList "
    cd '$PSScriptRoot\backend';
    py -m uvicorn backend.main:app --reload
" -WindowStyle Normal

Start-Sleep -Seconds 2

# --- Step 2: Start Next.js frontend ---
Write-Host "`n[2/2] Starting Next.js frontend..." -ForegroundColor Yellow

Start-Process powershell -ArgumentList "
    cd '$PSScriptRoot\superapp-frontend';
    npm run dev
" -WindowStyle Normal

Write-Host "`nSuperApp is now running!" -ForegroundColor Green
Write-Host "Backend:  http://localhost:8000"
Write-Host "Frontend: http://localhost:3000"
🧠 How it works
✔ Opens two PowerShell windows
One runs FastAPI

One runs Next.js

✔ Automatically navigates to the correct folders
✔ Works even if your Python is py instead of python
✔ Works even if your Next.js project is named differently (just adjust folder name)
▶️ How to run it
Save the script as:

Code


Copy
start-superapp.ps1
Right‑click → Run with PowerShell

OR run manually:

Copy

Copilot said
Sebastian — this one is easy to fix.
Your script is failing because inside the script, you used the command:

Code


Copy
powershell
But on your system, the correct executable is:

Code


Copy
pwsh
(or sometimes C:\Windows\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe)

That’s why PowerShell says:

Code


Copy
The term 'powershell' is not recognized
Let’s fix your script so it works on every Windows machine, including yours.

✅ Updated working script (use this one)
Save this as:

Code


Copy
start-superapp.ps1
Place it in your Superapp root folder.

powershell


Copy
# ================================
# SuperApp Startup Script
# Starts FastAPI backend + Next.js frontend
# ================================

Write-Host "Starting SuperApp..." -ForegroundColor Cyan

# Detect PowerShell executable
$psExe = $PSCommandPath
if ($PSVersionTable.PSEdition -eq "Core") {
    $shell = "pwsh"
} else {
    $shell = "$env:SystemRoot\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe"
}

# --- Step 1: Start FastAPI backend ---
Write-Host "`n[1/2] Starting FastAPI backend..." -ForegroundColor Yellow

Start-Process $shell -ArgumentList "
    cd '$PSScriptRoot\backend';
    py -m uvicorn backend.main:app --reload
" -WindowStyle Normal

Start-Sleep -Seconds 2

# --- Step 2: Start Next.js frontend ---
Write-Host "`n[2/2] Starting Next.js frontend..." -ForegroundColor Yellow

Start-Process $shell -ArgumentList "
    cd '$PSScriptRoot\superapp-frontend';
    npm run dev
" -WindowStyle Normal

Write-Host "`nSuperApp is now running!" -ForegroundColor Green
Write-Host "Backend:  http://localhost:8000"
Write-Host "Frontend: http://localhost:3000"
🧪 Now run it again
powershell


Copy
powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File .\start-superapp.ps1
If your system uses PowerShell Core (pwsh), run:

powershell


Copy
pwsh -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File .\start-superapp.ps1
🧠 Why this works
Your system doesn’t recognize the command powershell inside the script.
So we replaced it with a full path or pwsh, depending on what your system supports.

This guarantees:

Backend opens in a new window

Frontend opens in a new window

No more “powershell not recognized” errors

If it still fails
Tell me:

Your Windows version

The output of this command:

Copy

I’ll adjust the script perfectly for your machine.

# ================================
# SuperApp Startup Script
# Starts FastAPI backend + Next.js frontend
# ================================

Write-Host "Starting SuperApp..." -ForegroundColor Cyan

# Detect PowerShell executable
if ($PSVersionTable.PSEdition -eq "Core") {
    $shell = "pwsh"
} else {
    $shell = "$env:SystemRoot\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe"
}

# --- Step 1: Start FastAPI backend ---
Write-Host "`n[1/2] Starting FastAPI backend..." -ForegroundColor Yellow

Start-Process $shell -ArgumentList "
    cd '$PSScriptRoot\backend';
    py -m uvicorn backend.main:app --reload
" -WindowStyle Normal

Start-Sleep -Seconds 2

# --- Step 2: Start Next.js frontend ---
Write-Host "`n[2/2] Starting Next.js frontend..." -ForegroundColor Yellow

Start-Process $shell -ArgumentList "
    cd '$PSScriptRoot\frontend';
    npm run dev
" -WindowStyle Normal

Write-Host "`nSuperApp is now running!" -ForegroundColor Green
Write-Host "Backend:  http://localhost:8000"
Write-Host "Frontend: http://localhost:3000"
Save it.

Copilot said
Sebastian — this one is very common on Windows, and the fix is straightforward.
Your system is blocking PowerShell scripts, including npm.ps1, because of the Execution Policy.

Let’s fix it cleanly and safely.

✅ Fix Option 1 — Use the recommended safe command
Run this in PowerShell as Administrator:

powershell


Copy
Set-ExecutionPolicy RemoteSigned -Scope CurrentUser
Then try:

powershell


Copy
npm install
This is the safest and most common fix.
It allows local scripts (like npm) to run, but still blocks untrusted remote scripts.

✅ Fix Option 2 — Bypass only for this session (no permanent change)
If you prefer not to change system settings, run:

powershell


Copy
powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass
A new PowerShell window will open.

Inside that new window:

powershell


Copy
cd C:\Users\user\Superapp\frontend
npm install
This bypasses restrictions only for this session.

✅ Fix Option 3 — Run npm using node directly (bypasses PowerShell scripts entirely)
This avoids PowerShell policies completely:

powershell


Copy
node C:\Program Files\nodejs\node_modules\npm\bin\npm-cli.js install
Then start the dev server:

powershell


Copy
node C:\Program Files\nodejs\node_modules\npm\bin\npm-cli.js run dev
This works even if execution policies are locked down.

🧠 Why this happens
Windows PowerShell blocks scripts by default.
Node installs npm.ps1 into:

Code


Copy
C:\Program Files\nodejs\
PowerShell sees it as a script and blocks it unless execution policy allows it.

🎯 Recommended path for you
Since you're building a full-stack app and will run npm often, use:

powershell


Copy
Set-ExecutionPolicy RemoteSigned -Scope CurrentUser
This is safe, standard, and permanent for your user only.

Sebastian, this is a classic Windows PowerShell quirk — and the good news is: your system is accepting your input, but you're typing the answer in the wrong place.

Let me explain what’s happening and how to fix it cleanly.

✅ Why it keeps repeating the prompt
When PowerShell asks:

Code


Copy
Do you want to change the execution policy?
[Y] Yes  [A] Yes to All  [N] No  [L] No to All  [S] Suspend  [?] Help
…it expects you to type just the letter, like:

Code


Copy
Y
or

Code


Copy
A
But you typed:

Code


Copy
[A]
or

Code


Copy
[Y]
PowerShell treats [A] as invalid input, so it asks again.

That’s why it keeps looping.

🎯 How to answer correctly
When you see the prompt, type:

Code


Copy
A
and press Enter.

No brackets.
No quotes.
Just the letter.

🔧 If it STILL doesn’t change, use the guaranteed method
Run this exact command, which forces the change without prompting:

powershell


Copy
Set-ExecutionPolicy -Scope CurrentUser -ExecutionPolicy RemoteSigned -Force
The -Force flag skips the confirmation prompt entirely.

🧪 Verify it worked
Run:

Copy

You should see:

Code

          <Link href="/rides" className="hover:text-blue-600">Rides</Link>
          <Link href="/parcels" className="hover:text-blue-600">Parcels</Link>
          <Link href="/orders" className="hover:text-blue-600">Orders</Link>
          <Link href="/chargers" className="hover:text-blue-600">Chargers</Link>
          <Link href="/admin" className="hover:text-blue-600">Admin</Link>
          <Link href="/login" className="hover:text-blue-600 mt-6">Login</Link>
        </nav>
      </aside>

      {/* Main Content */}
      <main className="flex-1 p-10">{children}</main>
    </div>
  );
}

🌟 4. Add Authentication (Login + Signup)
/login/page.tsx
tsx


Copy
"use client";

import { useState } from "react";
import Layout from "@/components/Layout";

export default function Login() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [password, setPassword] = useState("");

  async function handleLogin(e: any) {
    e.preventDefault();

    const res = await fetch("http://localhost:8000/auth/login", {
      method: "POST",
      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
      body: JSON.stringify({ email, password }),
    });

    const data = await res.json();
    console.log(data);
  }

  return (
    <Layout>
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold mb-6">Login</h1>

      <form onSubmit={handleLogin} className="flex flex-col gap-4 max-w-sm">
        <input
          type="email"
          placeholder="Email"
          className="p-3 border rounded"
          value={email}
          onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
        />

        <input
          type="password"
          placeholder="Password"
          className="p-3 border rounded"
          value={password}
          onChange={(e) => setPassword(e.target.value)}
        />

        <button className="p-3 bg-blue-600 text-white rounded hover:bg-blue-700">
          Login
        </button>
      </form>
    </Layout>
  );
}
/signup/page.tsx
tsx


Copy

export default function Signup() {

    const res = await fetch("http://localhost:8000/auth/signup", {
      method: "POST",
      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
      body: JSON.stringify({ email, password }),
    });

    const data = await res.json();
    console.log(data);
  }

  return (

          type="email"
          placeholder="Email"
          className="p-3 border rounded"
          value={email}
          onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
        />

        <input
          type="password"

Edit in a page
You said

Layout.tsx
" this is not in the component its in the app
Copilot said
Ahh, I see exactly what happened — and you’re right to call it out.

In Next.js 13/14 with the App Router, components don’t live in /components unless you choose to put them there.
You can absolutely place Layout.tsx inside the app directory, and in fact, Next.js encourages layouts to live inside app/.

Let me show you the correct structure and the cleanest way to organize your SuperApp UI.

✅ Correct Next.js App Router Structure
Here’s how your project should look:

Code


Copy
frontend-app/
  app/
    layout.tsx        <-- Global layout for the entire app
    page.tsx          <-- Homepage
    restaurants/
      page.tsx
    rides/
      page.tsx
    parcels/
      page.tsx
    orders/
      page.tsx
    chargers/
      page.tsx
    admin/
      page.tsx
    login/
      page.tsx
    signup/
      page.tsx
  components/
    Sidebar.tsx       <-- Optional: reusable sidebar component
So yes — your layout belongs in app/layout.tsx, not in /components.

🎯 Here is the correct app/layout.tsx for your SuperApp
Replace your existing app/layout.tsx with this:

tsx


Copy
import "./globals.css";
import Sidebar from "@/components/Sidebar";

export const metadata = {
  title: "SuperApp",
  description: "All-in-one services dashboard",
};

export default function RootLayout({
  children,
}: {
  children: React.ReactNode;
}) {
  return (
    <html lang="en">
      <body className="flex min-h-screen bg-gray-100">
        <Sidebar />
        <main className="flex-1 p-10">{children}</main>
      </body>
    </html>
  );
}
This makes the sidebar global across all pages.

  return (
    <aside className="w-64 bg-white shadow-md p-6 flex flex-col gap-4">
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold text-blue-600">SuperApp</h1>

      <nav className="flex flex-col gap-3 text-lg">
        <Link href="/" className="hover:text-blue-600">Home</Link>
        <Link href="/restaurants" className="hover:text-blue-600">Restaurants</Link>
        <Link href="/rides" className="hover:text-blue-600">Rides</Link>
        <Link href="/parcels" className="hover:text-blue-600">Parcels</Link>
        <Link href="/orders" className="hover:text-blue-600">Orders</Link>
        <Link href="/chargers" className="hover:text-blue-600">Chargers</Link>
        <Link href="/admin" className="hover:text-blue-600">Admin</Link>

        <div className="mt-6 border-t pt-4">
          <Link href="/login" className="hover:text-blue-600">Login</Link>
          <Link href="/signup" className="hover:text-blue-600">Signup</Link>
        </div>
      </nav>
    </aside>
  );
}
🎯 Your homepage stays in app/page.tsx
This file now only renders the dashboard content, because the layout + sidebar are global.

🧠 Why this is correct
In the App Router, layouts belong inside the app/ directory because:

They wrap all routes automatically

They persist across navigation

They support streaming and partial rendering

They are part of the routing tree

Putting Layout.tsx inside /components would break this behavior.

2. components/Sidebar.tsx
Create this file:

tsx


Copy
// components/Sidebar.tsx
"use client";

import Link from "next/link";
import { usePathname } from "next/navigation";
import clsx from "clsx";

const navItems = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/" },
  { label: "Restaurants", href: "/restaurants" },
  { label: "Rides", href: "/rides" },
  { label: "Parcels", href: "/parcels" },
  { label: "Orders", href: "/orders" },
  { label: "Chargers", href: "/chargers" },
  { label: "Admin", href: "/admin" },
];

export default function Sidebar() {
  const pathname = usePathname();

  return (
    <aside className="w-64 bg-white shadow-md p-6 flex flex-col gap-4">
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold text-blue-600 mb-4">SuperApp</h1>

      <nav className="flex flex-col gap-2 text-sm">
        {navItems.map((item) => (
          <Link
            key={item.href}
            href={item.href}
            className={clsx(
              "rounded px-3 py-2 transition-colors",
              pathname === item.href
                ? "bg-blue-600 text-white"
                : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
            )}
          >
            {item.label}
          </Link>
        ))}
      </nav>

      <div className="mt-auto border-t pt-4 flex flex-col gap-2 text-sm">
        <Link
          href="/login"
          className={clsx(
            "rounded px-3 py-2 transition-colors",
            pathname === "/login"
              ? "bg-blue-600 text-white"
              : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
          )}
        >
          Login
        </Link>
        <Link
          href="/signup"
          className={clsx(
            "rounded px-3 py-2 transition-colors",
            pathname === "/signup"
              ? "bg-blue-600 text-white"
              : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
          )}
        >
          Signup
        </Link>
      </div>
    </aside>
  );
}

5. Auth pages: login + signup
These are wired to your future FastAPI auth endpoints.

app/login/page.tsx
tsx


Copy
// app/login/page.tsx
"use client";

import { useState } from "react";

export default function LoginPage() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [password, setPassword] = useState("");
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);

  async function handleSubmit(e: React.FormEvent) {
    e.preventDefault();
    setLoading(true);
    setError(null);

    try {
      const res = await fetch("http://localhost:8000/auth/login", {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
        body: JSON.stringify({ email, password }),
      });

      if (!res.ok) {
        const err = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));
        throw new Error(err.detail || "Login failed");
      }

      const data = await res.json();
      console.log("Login success:", data);
      // TODO: store token, redirect
    } catch (err: any) {
      setError(err.message || "Login failed");
    } finally {
      setLoading(false);
    }
  }

  return (
    <div className="max-w-sm mx-auto">
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold mb-4">Login</h1>
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="flex flex-col gap-4">
        <input
          type="email"
          placeholder="Email"
          className="p-3 border rounded text-sm"
          value={email}
          onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
          required
        />

        <input
          type="password"
          placeholder="Password"
          className="p-3 border rounded text-sm"
          value={password}
          onChange={(e) => setPassword(e.target.value)}
          required
        />

        {error && <p className="text-sm text-red-600">{error}</p>}

        <button
          type="submit"
          disabled={loading}
          className="p-3 bg-blue-600 text-white rounded text-sm hover:bg-blue-700 disabled:opacity-60"
        >
          {loading ? "Logging in..." : "Login"}
        </button>
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
app/signup/page.tsx
tsx


Copy
// app/signup/page.tsx
"use client";

import { useState } from "react";

export default function SignupPage() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [password, setPassword] = useState("");
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);
  const [success, setSuccess] = useState<string | null>(null);

  async function handleSubmit(e: React.FormEvent) {
    e.preventDefault();
    setLoading(true);
    setError(null);
    setSuccess(null);

    try {
      const res = await fetch("http://localhost:8000/auth/signup", {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
        body: JSON.stringify({ email, password }),
      });

      if (!res.ok) {
        const err = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));
        throw new Error(err.detail || "Signup failed");
      }

      const data = await res.json();
      console.log("Signup success:", data);
      setSuccess("Account created successfully. You can now log in.");
    } catch (err: any) {
      setError(err.message || "Signup failed");
    } finally {
      setLoading(false);
    }
  }

  return (
    <div className="max-w-sm mx-auto">
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold mb-4">Create account</h1>
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="flex flex-col gap-4">
        <input
          type="email"
          placeholder="Email"
          className="p-3 border rounded text-sm"
          value={email}
          onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
          required
        />

        <input
          type="password"
          placeholder="Password"
          className="p-3 border rounded text-sm"
          value={password}
          onChange={(e) => setPassword(e.target.value)}
          required
        />

        {error && <p className="text-sm text-red-600">{error}</p>}
        {success && <p className="text-sm text-green-600">{success}</p>}

        <button
          type="submit"
          disabled={loading}
          className="p-3 bg-green-600 text-white rounded text-sm hover:bg-green-700 disabled:opacity-60"
        >
          {loading ? "Creating account..." : "Sign up"}
        </button>
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}

🎨 2. Upgrade the Sidebar with icons + better styling
Replace your Sidebar.tsx with this improved version:

tsx


Copy
"use client";

import Link from "next/link";
import { usePathname } from "next/navigation";
import clsx from "clsx";

import {
  HomeIcon,
  BuildingStorefrontIcon,
  TruckIcon,
  BoltIcon,
  Cog6ToothIcon,
  MapIcon,
  UserIcon,
} from "@heroicons/react/24/outline";

const navItems = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  { label: "Restaurants", href: "/restaurants", icon: BuildingStorefrontIcon },
  { label: "Rides", href: "/rides", icon: MapIcon },
  { label: "Parcels", href: "/parcels", icon: TruckIcon },
  { label: "Orders", href: "/orders", icon: Cog6ToothIcon },
  { label: "Chargers", href: "/chargers", icon: BoltIcon },
  { label: "Admin", href: "/admin", icon: UserIcon },
];

export default function Sidebar() {
  const pathname = usePathname();

  return (
    <aside className="w-64 bg-white shadow-lg p-6 flex flex-col gap-6 border-r border-gray-200">
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold text-blue-600 tracking-tight">
        SuperApp
      </h1>

      <nav className="flex flex-col gap-2">
        {navItems.map((item) => (
          <Link
            key={item.href}
            href={item.href}
            className={clsx(
              "flex items-center gap-3 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg transition-all",
              pathname === item.href
                ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
                : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
            )}
          >
            <item.icon className="h-5 w-5" />
            {item.label}
          </Link>
        ))}
      </nav>

      <div className="mt-auto border-t pt-4 flex flex-col gap-2">
        <Link
          href="/login"
          className={clsx(
            "flex items-center gap-3 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg transition-all",
            pathname === "/login"
              ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
              : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
          )}
        >
          <UserIcon className="h-5 w-5" />
          Login
        </Link>

        <Link
          href="/signup"
          className={clsx(
            "flex items-center gap-3 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg transition-all",
            pathname === "/signup"
              ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
              : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
          )}
        >
          <UserIcon className="h-5 w-5" />
          Signup
        </Link>
      </div>
    </aside>
  );
}
This gives you:

Clean icons

Highlighted active route

Better spacing

Modern sidebar look

const cards = [
  {
    title: "Restaurants",

  },
  {
    title: "Parcels",
    description: "Send and track deliveries",
    href: "/parcels",
    icon: "📦",
  },
  {
    title: "Orders",

  title: "SuperApp",
  description: "All-in-one services dashboard",
};

export default function RootLayout({
  children,
}: {
  children: React.ReactNode;
}) {
  return (
    <html lang="en">
      <body className="flex min-h-screen bg-gray-100">
        <Sidebar />
        <main className="flex-1 p-10">{children}</main>
      </body>
    </html>
  );
}
If you forgot to wrap with <Sidebar />, the component compiles but never appears.

4. Check for TypeScript issues
If you’re using TypeScript and seeing errors in the editor like JSX element type 'item.icon' does not have any construct or call signatures, you can help the type system by typing navItems:

tsx


Copy
type NavItem = {
  label: string;
  href: string;
  icon: (props: React.SVGProps<SVGSVGElement>) => JSX.Element;
};

const navItems: NavItem[] = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  // etc...
];
If you’re in JS, you don’t need this.

Copilot said
Sebastian — I know exactly what this error means, and it’s not your fault.
This happens when Tailwind is not initialized correctly, and your globals.css is being treated as a normal CSS file instead of a Tailwind file.

The key clue is here:

Code


Copy
Cannot apply unknown utility class `text-3xl`
Tailwind doesn’t even recognize its own classes — which means Tailwind is not running.

Let’s fix this cleanly and permanently.

✅ STEP 1 — Your globals.css is wrong
You likely added this:

css


Copy
h1 {
  @apply text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight;
}
But Tailwind cannot process @apply unless Tailwind is properly configured.

For now, REMOVE everything except the Tailwind directives.

Your app/globals.css must be EXACTLY this:

css


Copy
@tailwind base;
@tailwind components;
@tailwind utilities;
Nothing else.

Save the file.

✅ STEP 2 — Fix your tailwind.config.js
Open:

Code


Copy
frontend-app/tailwind.config.js
It MUST contain this:

js


Copy
/** @type {import('tailwindcss').Config} */
module.exports = {
  content: [
    "./app/**/*.{js,ts,jsx,tsx}",
    "./components/**/*.{js,ts,jsx,tsx}",
  ],
  theme: {
    extend: {},
  },
  plugins: [],
};
If content is wrong, Tailwind won’t scan your files → all classes break.

✅ STEP 3 — Fix your postcss.config.js
Open:

Code


Copy
frontend-app/postcss.config.js
It MUST be:

js


Copy
module.exports = {
  plugins: {
    tailwindcss: {},
    autoprefixer: {},
  },
};
If Tailwind isn’t listed here, it never runs.

✅ STEP 4 — Restart the dev server
This is important.

Stop the server:

Code


Copy
CTRL + C
Then restart:

Code


Copy
npm run dev
Tailwind will now rebuild correctly.

🎉 After this, Tailwind utilities like text-3xl, bg-white, flex, etc. will work perfectly.
⚠️ WHY THIS HAPPENED
You added this earlier:

css


Copy
h1 {
  @apply text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight;
}
But Tailwind wasn’t fully initialized yet, so PostCSS threw an error.

We’ll re-add typography later — but only after Tailwind is confirmed working.

Copilot said
Sebastian — this file is the exact reason Tailwind is crashing.  
You’ve mixed custom CSS, Tailwind directives, and @apply rules in the wrong order, and you duplicated blocks.

Let me break down the issues clearly and fix them cleanly.

❌ What’s wrong in your current globals.css
1. Tailwind directives must be at the TOP of the file
Tailwind requires:

css


Copy
@tailwind base;
@tailwind components;
@tailwind utilities;
to appear before any custom CSS.

Right now, they’re at the bottom → Tailwind can’t process your @apply.

2. You duplicated your :root and body blocks
You have them twice.

3. You used @apply before Tailwind was initialized
This triggers:

Code


Copy
CssSyntaxError: Cannot apply unknown utility class `text-3xl`
✅ Here is the correct, fixed globals.css
Copy–paste this EXACT version:

css


Copy
/* ----------------------------- */
/* 1. Tailwind must come first   */
/* ----------------------------- */
@tailwind base;
@tailwind components;
@tailwind utilities;

/* ----------------------------- */
/* 2. Design tokens (your vars)  */
/* ----------------------------- */
:root {
  --primary: #2563eb;
  --primary-light: #3b82f6;
  --primary-dark: #1e40af;

  --bg: #f8fafc;
  --card: #ffffff;
  --border: #e2e8f0;
}

/* ----------------------------- */
/* 3. Global styles              */
/* ----------------------------- */
body {
  background: var(--bg);
}

/* ----------------------------- */
/* 4. Typography using @apply    */
/* ----------------------------- */
h1 {
  @apply text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight;
}

h2 {
  @apply text-xl font-semibold;
}

p {
  @apply text-gray-600;
}

Next.js is telling you that another Next.js dev server is still running in the background, holding a lock on:

Code


Copy
C:\Users\user\Superapp\frontend-app\.next\dev\lock
Even though you closed the terminal, the process is still alive.

Let’s kill it cleanly.

✅ Fix Step 1 — Find the stuck Next.js process
Run this in PowerShell:

powershell


Copy

You will see one or more Node.js processes.

✅ Fix Step 2 — Kill all Node processes
Run:

powershell


Copy

This force‑kills any leftover Next.js dev servers.

✅ Fix Step 3 — Delete the stale lock file
Sometimes the lock file remains even after killing the process.

Run:

powershell


Copy
Remove-Item -Force -Path ".next\dev\lock"
If Windows complains the file is in use, it means a Node process is still running — repeat Step 2.

✅ Fix Step 4 — Restart the dev server
Now run:

powershell


Copy
npm run dev
It should start cleanly on port 3000 or 3001.

⚠️ Why this happened
Next.js (Turbopack) creates a lock file to prevent two dev servers from running in the same folder.
If the previous server crashed or the terminal closed abruptly, the lock stays behind.

This is normal on Windows.

"use client";

import Link from "next/link";
import { usePathname } from "next/navigation";
import clsx from "clsx";

import {
  HomeIcon,
  BuildingStorefrontIcon,
  TruckIcon,
  BoltIcon,
  Cog6ToothIcon,
  MapIcon,
  UserIcon,
} from "@heroicons/react/24/outline";

const navItems = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  { label: "Restaurants", href: "/restaurants", icon: BuildingStorefrontIcon },
  { label: "Rides", href: "/rides", icon: MapIcon },
  { label: "Parcels", href: "/parcels", icon: TruckIcon },
  { label: "Orders", href: "/orders", icon: Cog6ToothIcon },
  { label: "Chargers", href: "/chargers", icon: BoltIcon },
  { label: "Admin", href: "/admin", icon: UserIcon },
];

export default function Sidebar() {
  const pathname = usePathname();

  return (
    <aside className="w-64 bg-white shadow-lg p-6 flex flex-col gap-6 border-r border-gray-200">
      <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold text-blue-600 tracking-tight">
        SuperApp
      </h1>

      <nav className="flex flex-col gap-2">
        {navItems.map((item) => (
          <Link
            key={item.href}
            href={item.href}
            className={clsx(
              "flex items-center gap-3 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg transition-all",
              pathname === item.href
                ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
                : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
            )}
          >
            <item.icon className="h-5 w-5" />
            {item.label}
          </Link>
        ))}
      </nav>

      <div className="mt-auto border-t pt-4 flex flex-col gap-2">
        <Link
          href="/login"
          className={clsx(
            "flex items-center gap-3 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg transition-all",
            pathname === "/login"
              ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
              : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
          )}
        >
          <UserIcon className="h-5 w-5" />
          Login
        </Link>

        <Link
          href="/signup"
          className={clsx(
            "flex items-center gap-3 px-3 py-2 rounded-lg transition-all",
            pathname === "/signup"
              ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
              : "text-gray-700 hover:bg-gray-100"
          )}
        >
          <UserIcon className="h-5 w-5" />
          Signup
        </Link>
      </div>
    </aside>
  );
}

✅ What package‑lock.json is
package-lock.json is automatically created by npm.
It:

locks exact dependency versions

ensures consistent installs

is not edited manually

is not related to your Tailwind error

is not the cause of your build failing

So don’t delete it, don’t modify it — just leave it alone.

1. Tailwind is not configured correctly

package-lock.json has nothing to do with any of this.

Copilot said
Sebastian — this one is finally simple.  
Your Tailwind nightmare is over, and now you’re just seeing a pure JavaScript error:

Code


Copy
HomeIcon is not defined
This means:

⭐ You are using HomeIcon in layout.tsx, but you did NOT import it there.
You imported the icons in Sidebar.tsx, but you are ALSO referencing them in layout.tsx, and layout.tsx has no import for them.

Next.js is telling you:

“You’re trying to use HomeIcon, but I don’t know what that variable is.”

Let’s fix it cleanly.

✅ Fix Option 1 — Import the icons inside layout.tsx
At the top of app/layout.tsx, add:

tsx


Copy
import {
  HomeIcon,
  BuildingStorefrontIcon,
  TruckIcon,
  BoltIcon,
  Cog6ToothIcon,
  MapIcon,
  UserIcon,
} from "@heroicons/react/24/outline";
This matches what you already have in Sidebar.tsx.

✅ Fix Option 2 — Remove icons from layout.tsx entirely
If your navItems array belongs in the sidebar, not layout, then layout.tsx should NOT define nav items at all.

You can safely delete this block from layout.tsx:

tsx


Copy
const navItems: NavItem[] = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  // ...
];
Because your sidebar already defines its own nav items.

This is actually the cleaner architecture:

Sidebar.tsx → contains nav items + icons

layout.tsx → wraps the page and renders <Sidebar />

No duplication.

🎯 Which fix should you choose?
✔ If layout.tsx is NOT supposed to contain nav items
→ Delete the navItems array from layout.tsx  
→ Sidebar handles navigation
→ Cleanest structure

✔ If layout.tsx should contain nav items
→ Add the missing imports  
→ No more ReferenceError

Step 1: Replace your Sidebar with a polished version
Create or update components/Sidebar.tsx with this code:

tsx


Copy
"use client";

import Link from "next/link";
import { usePathname } from "next/navigation";
import clsx from "clsx";

import {
  HomeIcon,
  BuildingStorefrontIcon,
  TruckIcon,
  BoltIcon,
  Cog6ToothIcon,
  MapIcon,
  UserIcon,
} from "@heroicons/react/24/outline";

type NavItem = {
  label: string;
  href: string;
  icon: React.ComponentType<React.SVGProps<SVGSVGElement>>;
};

const navItems: NavItem[] = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  { label: "Businesses", href: "/businesses", icon: BuildingStorefrontIcon },
  { label: "Logistics", href: "/logistics", icon: TruckIcon },
  { label: "Energy", href: "/energy", icon: BoltIcon },
  { label: "Map", href: "/map", icon: MapIcon },
  { label: "Account", href: "/account", icon: UserIcon },
  { label: "Settings", href: "/settings", icon: Cog6ToothIcon },
];

export function Sidebar() {
  const pathname = usePathname();

  return (
    <aside className="flex h-screen w-64 flex-col border-r border-slate-200 bg-white/80 backdrop-blur">
      {/* Brand */}
      <div className="flex items-center gap-2 px-6 py-5 border-b border-slate-200">
        <div className="flex h-9 w-9 items-center justify-center rounded-xl bg-blue-600 text-white font-semibold">
          SA
        </div>
        <div className="flex flex-col">
          <span className="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-900">
            SuperApp
          </span>
          <span className="text-xs text-slate-500">
            Mobility • Energy • Finance
          </span>
        </div>
      </div>

      {/* Nav */}
      <nav className="flex-1 px-3 py-4 space-y-1 overflow-y-auto">
        {navItems.map((item) => {
          const Icon = item.icon;
          const isActive =
            pathname === item.href ||
            (item.href !== "/" && pathname.startsWith(item.href));

          return (
            <Link
              key={item.href}
              href={item.href}
              className={clsx(
                "group flex items-center gap-3 rounded-lg px-3 py-2.5 text-sm font-medium transition-colors",
                "hover:bg-blue-50 hover:text-blue-700",
                isActive
                  ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
                  : "text-slate-600"
              )}
            >
              <Icon
                className={clsx(
                  "h-5 w-5",
                  isActive
                    ? "text-white"
                    : "text-slate-400 group-hover:text-blue-600"
                )}
              />
              <span>{item.label}</span>
            </Link>
          );
        })}
      </nav>

      {/* Bottom section (user / status / version) */}
      <div className="border-t border-slate-200 px-4 py-3 text-xs text-slate-500">
        <div className="flex items-center justify-between">
          <span>v0.1.0</span>
          <span className="rounded-full bg-emerald-50 px-2 py-0.5 text-[11px] font-medium text-emerald-700">
            Live
          </span>
        </div>
      </div>
    </aside>
  );
}
This gives you:

Brand block (logo initials + tagline)

Clean nav with icons

Active route highlighting using usePathname

Hover states and subtle transitions

Bottom status strip (version + “Live”)

      <body className="bg-slate-50 text-slate-900">
        <div className="flex min-h-screen">
          <Sidebar />
          <main className="flex-1 p-6">{children}</main>
        </div>
      </body>
    </html>
  );
}

Copilot said
Got you, Sebastian — this error is almost always caused by one of three things, and we can fix it in under a minute.

Let’s walk through it cleanly.

🎯 THE ERROR MEANS:
Next.js cannot find or load your Sidebar component.

The arrow points to:

tsx


Copy
<Sidebar />
Which means the import is failing.

✅ Step 1 — Check your import path
You currently have:

tsx


Copy
import Sidebar from "@/components/Sidebar";
This only works if:

✔ You have a folder:
Code


Copy
/components/Sidebar.tsx
✔ And your tsconfig.json has:
json


Copy
"paths": {
  "@/*": ["./*"]
}
If the file exists but the alias is not configured, Next.js will throw exactly the error you’re seeing.

🔧 Fix Option A — Use a relative import (guaranteed to work)
Replace:

tsx


Copy
import Sidebar from "@/components/Sidebar";
with:

tsx


Copy
import Sidebar from "../components/Sidebar";
or, depending on your folder structure:

tsx


Copy
import Sidebar from "../../components/Sidebar";
Since layout.tsx is inside /app, the correct path is:

tsx


Copy
import Sidebar from "../components/Sidebar";
This is the simplest and most reliable fix.

🔧 Fix Option B — Enable the @ alias (optional but cleaner)
Open tsconfig.json and ensure you have:

json


Copy
{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "baseUrl": ".",
    "paths": {
      "@/*": ["./*"]
    }
  }
}
Then restart your dev server.

This makes @/components/Sidebar work everywhere.

🧪 Step 2 — Confirm Sidebar is a default export
In components/Sidebar.tsx, make sure you have:

tsx


Copy
export default function Sidebar() {
  ...
}
If you used:

tsx


Copy
export function Sidebar() { ... }
Then you must import it like:

tsx


Copy
import { Sidebar } from "../components/Sidebar";
Mismatch = error.

🟢 Step 3 — Restart the dev server
Next.js caches module resolution, so run:

powershell


Copy
npm run dev
🚀 Tell me what you see after applying Fix A
If you paste your folder structure like this:

Code


Copy
frontend-app/
  app/
    layout.tsx
  components/
    Sidebar.tsx
I’ll confirm the exact import path for you.

Check the render method of `RootLayout`.
app\layout.tsx (18:11) @ RootLayout

Show 15 ignore-listed frame(s)
RootLayout
app\layout.tsx (18:11)"
Copilot said
Sebastian — this error is 100% caused by one thing:

👉 Sidebar is undefined at runtime.
And React is telling you:

“You tried to render <Sidebar />, but the thing you imported is not a component.”

This ALWAYS comes from one of these three causes:

✅ Cause 1 — Wrong import (most common)
You currently have:

ts


Copy
import Sidebar from "@/components/Sidebar";
But your actual file might export it like:

ts


Copy
export function Sidebar() { ... }
If that’s the case, then the import MUST be:

ts


Copy
import { Sidebar } from "@/components/Sidebar";
✔ Default export → import Sidebar from ...
✔ Named export → import { Sidebar } from ...
If these don’t match, React throws the exact error you’re seeing.

✅ Cause 2 — Wrong file path
Your folder structure MUST look like:

Code


Copy
frontend-app/
  app/
    layout.tsx
  components/
    Sidebar.tsx
If your Sidebar is actually inside:

Code


Copy
app/components/Sidebar.tsx
Then the correct import is:

ts


Copy
import Sidebar from "./components/Sidebar";
If it’s inside:

Code


Copy
src/components/Sidebar.tsx
Then:

ts


Copy
import Sidebar from "@/components/Sidebar";
If the path is wrong → Sidebar = undefined → error.

✅ Cause 3 — Sidebar file has a syntax error or missing export
Open components/Sidebar.tsx and confirm the VERY TOP looks like:

tsx


Copy
"use client";

export default function Sidebar() {
  return (
    <aside>
      ...
    </aside>
  );
}
If you see:

tsx


Copy
export function Sidebar() { ... }
Then you must import it with curly braces.

If you see:

tsx


Copy
function Sidebar() { ... }
with no export, then Sidebar is undefined.

"use client";

import Link from "next/link";
import { usePathname } from "next/navigation";
import clsx from "clsx";

import {
  HomeIcon,
  BuildingStorefrontIcon,
  TruckIcon,
  BoltIcon,
  Cog6ToothIcon,
  MapIcon,
  UserIcon,
} from "@heroicons/react/24/outline";

type NavItem = {
  label: string;
  href: string;
  icon: React.ComponentType<React.SVGProps<SVGSVGElement>>;
};

const navItems: NavItem[] = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  { label: "Businesses", href: "/businesses", icon: BuildingStorefrontIcon },
  { label: "Logistics", href: "/logistics", icon: TruckIcon },
  { label: "Energy", href: "/energy", icon: BoltIcon },
  { label: "Map", href: "/map", icon: MapIcon },
  { label: "Account", href: "/account", icon: UserIcon },
  { label: "Settings", href: "/settings", icon: Cog6ToothIcon },
];

export default function Sidebar() {
  const pathname = usePathname();

  return (
    <aside className="flex h-screen w-64 flex-col border-r border-slate-200 bg-white/80 backdrop-blur">
      {/* Brand */}
      <div className="flex items-center gap-2 px-6 py-5 border-b border-slate-200">
        <div className="flex h-9 w-9 items-center justify-center rounded-xl bg-blue-600 text-white font-semibold">
          SA
        </div>
        <div className="flex flex-col">
          <span className="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-900">
            SuperApp
          </span>
          <span className="text-xs text-slate-500">
            Mobility • Energy • Finance
          </span>
        </div>
      </div>

      {/* Navigation */}
      <nav className="flex-1 px-3 py-4 space-y-1 overflow-y-auto">
        {navItems.map((item) => {
          const Icon = item.icon;
          const isActive =
            pathname === item.href ||
            (item.href !== "/" && pathname.startsWith(item.href));

          return (
            <Link
              key={item.href}
              href={item.href}
              className={clsx(
                "group flex items-center gap-3 rounded-lg px-3 py-2.5 text-sm font-medium transition-colors",
                "hover:bg-blue-50 hover:text-blue-700",
                isActive
                  ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
                  : "text-slate-600"
              )}
            >
              <Icon
                className={clsx(
                  "h-5 w-5",
                  isActive
                    ? "text-white"
                    : "text-slate-400 group-hover:text-blue-600"
                )}
              />
              <span>{item.label}</span>
            </Link>
          );
        })}
      </nav>

      {/* Footer */}
      <div className="border-t border-slate-200 px-4 py-3 text-xs text-slate-500">
        <div className="flex items-center justify-between">
          <span>v0.1.0</span>
          <span className="rounded-full bg-emerald-50 px-2 py-0.5 text-[11px] font-medium text-emerald-700">
            Live
          </span>
        </div>
      </div>
    </aside>
  );
}

Edit in a page
You said

Missing <html> and <body> tags in the root layout
Copilot said
Sebastian — this error is very specific, and it tells us exactly what’s wrong:

🚨 Next.js is NOT seeing your <html> and <body> tags
Even though you did write them.

This happens when your layout file exports something invalid, or when extra code appears after the layout, causing Next.js to ignore the layout wrapper.

And guess what?
You did have extra code after the layout earlier:

ts


Copy

"use client";

import Link from "next/link";
import { usePathname } from "next/navigation";
import clsx from "clsx";

import {
  HomeIcon,
  BuildingStorefrontIcon,
  TruckIcon,
  BoltIcon,
  Cog6ToothIcon,
  MapIcon,
  UserIcon,
} from "@heroicons/react/24/outline";

type NavItem = {
  label: string;
  href: string;
  icon: React.ComponentType<React.SVGProps<SVGSVGElement>>;
};

const navItems: NavItem[] = [
  { label: "Home", href: "/", icon: HomeIcon },
  { label: "Businesses", href: "/businesses", icon: BuildingStorefrontIcon },
  { label: "Logistics", href: "/logistics", icon: TruckIcon },
  { label: "Energy", href: "/energy", icon: BoltIcon },
  { label: "Map", href: "/map", icon: MapIcon },
  { label: "Account", href: "/account", icon: UserIcon },
  { label: "Settings", href: "/settings", icon: Cog6ToothIcon },
];

export default function Sidebar() {
  const pathname = usePathname();

  return (
    <aside className="flex h-screen w-64 flex-col border-r border-slate-200 bg-white/80 backdrop-blur">
      {/* Brand */}
      <div className="flex items-center gap-2 px-6 py-5 border-b border-slate-200">
        <div className="flex h-9 w-9 items-center justify-center rounded-xl bg-blue-600 text-white font-semibold">
          SA
        </div>
        <div className="flex flex-col">
          <span className="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-900">
            SuperApp
          </span>
          <span className="text-xs text-slate-500">
            Mobility • Energy • Finance
          </span>
        </div>
      </div>

      {/* Navigation */}
      <nav className="flex-1 px-3 py-4 space-y-1 overflow-y-auto">
        {navItems.map((item) => {
          const Icon = item.icon;
          const isActive =
            pathname === item.href ||
            (item.href !== "/" && pathname.startsWith(item.href));

          return (
            <Link
              key={item.href}
              href={item.href}
              className={clsx(
                "group flex items-center gap-3 rounded-lg px-3 py-2.5 text-sm font-medium transition-colors",
                "hover:bg-blue-50 hover:text-blue-700",
                isActive
                  ? "bg-blue-600 text-white shadow-sm"
                  : "text-slate-600"
              )}
            >
              <Icon
                className={clsx(
                  "h-5 w-5",
                  isActive
                    ? "text-white"
                    : "text-slate-400 group-hover:text-blue-600"
                )}
              />
              <span>{item.label}</span>
            </Link>
          );
        })}
      </nav>

      {/* Footer */}
      <div className="border-t border-slate-200 px-4 py-3 text-xs text-slate-500">
        <div className="flex items-center justify-between">
          <span>v0.1.0</span>
          <span className="rounded-full bg-emerald-50 px-2 py-0.5 text-[11px] font-medium text-emerald-700">
            Live
          </span>
        </div>
      </div>
    </aside>
  );
}

Copilot said
Sebastian — I see exactly what’s happening now.

You’re asking me to insert <html> and <body> tags into the Sidebar code, but that is NOT allowed in Next.js.

❗ Important rule in Next.js App Router:
<html> and <body> must ONLY appear in app/layout.tsx

They must NOT appear in components like Sidebar.tsx

If you insert <html> or <body> inside Sidebar, Next.js will break.

So the correct structure is:

Sidebar.tsx → only the sidebar component

layout.tsx → contains <html> and <body>

You already have the correct Sidebar code.
Now I will give you the correct full layout.tsx with <html> and <body> included.

⭐ Step-by-step plan (clean and scalable)
STEP 1 — Add Authentication (NextAuth.js)
This is the industry standard for Next.js 13/14/15/16.

It gives you:

Email/password login

OAuth (Google, Apple, etc.)

JWT sessions

Role-based access

Server-side protection

Install:
bash


Copy
npm install next-auth
Create the auth route:
Code


Copy
app/api/auth/[...nextauth]/route.ts
Inside:

ts


Copy
import NextAuth from "next-auth";
import CredentialsProvider from "next-auth/providers/credentials";

const handler = NextAuth({
  providers: [
    CredentialsProvider({
      name: "Credentials",
      credentials: {
        email: {},
        password: {},
      },
      async authorize(credentials) {
        // TODO: Replace with real DB lookup
        if (
          credentials?.email === "test@example.com" &&
          credentials?.password === "password"
        ) {
          return {
            id: "1",
            name: "Test User",
            role: "user",
          };
        }
        return null;
      },
    }),
  ],
  callbacks: {
    async jwt({ token, user }) {
      if (user) token.role = user.role;
      return token;
    },
    async session({ session, token }) {
      session.user.role = token.role;
      return session;
    },
  },
});

export { handler as GET, handler as POST };
This gives you:

Login

Session

Role stored in JWT

⭐ STEP 2 — Add Login Page

Code

Copy
"use client";

import { signIn } from "next-auth/react";
import { useState } from "react";

export default function LoginPage() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [password, setPassword] = useState("");

  async function handleLogin(e: any) {
    e.preventDefault();
    await signIn("credentials", {
      email,
      password,
      callbackUrl: "/",
    });
  }

  return (
    <div className="flex items-center justify-center min-h-screen bg-slate-100">
      <form
        onSubmit={handleLogin}
        className="bg-white p-8 rounded-xl shadow-md w-80 space-y-4"
      >
        <h1 className="text-xl font-semibold">Login</h1>

        <input
          className="w-full border rounded px-3 py-2"
          placeholder="Email"
          onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
        />

        <input
          type="password"
          className="w-full border rounded px-3 py-2"
          placeholder="Password"
          onChange={(e) => setPassword(e.target.value)}
        />

        <button
          type="submit"
          className="w-full bg-blue-600 text-white py-2 rounded"
        >
          Sign In
        </button>
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
⭐ STEP 3 — Protect Routes (Only logged-in users can access dashboard)

Code


Copy
app/(protected)/layout.tsx
tsx


Copy
import { getServerSession } from "next-auth";
import { redirect } from "next/navigation";

export default async function ProtectedLayout({ children }) {
  const session = await getServerSession();

  if (!session) redirect("/login");

  return <>{children}</>;
}
Now any page inside (protected) requires login.

Great question, Sebastian — and this is one of those places where Next.js App Router structure matters a lot.
Let me walk you through it cleanly so you put the file in the exact correct place.

📌 Where to create app/api/auth/[...nextauth]/route.ts
You will create it inside your Next.js App Router API folder, like this:

Code


Copy
app/
  api/
    auth/
      [...nextauth]/
        route.ts
So the full path is:

Code


Copy
/app/api/auth/[...nextauth]/route.ts
This is the official Next.js 13–16 way of defining API routes.

🧭 How to create it step-by-step
1. Go to your project root
This is the folder containing:

Code


Copy
app/
components/
package.json
2. Inside app/, create a folder named api
Code


Copy
app/api/
3. Inside api/, create a folder named auth
Code


Copy
app/api/auth/
4. Inside auth/, create a folder named [...nextauth]
Code


Copy
app/api/auth/[...nextauth]/
5. Inside [...nextauth]/, create a file named:
Code


Copy
route.ts
🧩 Your final folder structure should look like this:
Code


Copy
app/
  layout.tsx
  page.tsx

  api/
    auth/
      [...nextauth]/
        route.ts

components/
  Sidebar.tsx
This is exactly how Next.js expects API routes to be structured.

🔥 Why this location matters
Next.js App Router uses:

app/**/page.tsx → pages

app/**/layout.tsx → layouts

app/api/**/route.ts → API endpoints

So:

Code


Copy
app/api/auth/[...nextauth]/route.ts
becomes your authentication endpoint at:

Code


Copy
/api/auth/[...nextauth]
NextAuth automatically hooks into this.

"use client";

import { useState } from "react";

export default function LoginPage() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [password, setPassword] = useState("");
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);

  async function handleSubmit(e: React.FormEvent) {
    e.preventDefault();
    setLoading(true);
    setError(null);

      const res = await fetch("http://localhost:8000/auth/login", {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
        body: JSON.stringify({ email, password }),
      });

      if (!res.ok) {
        const err = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));
        throw new Error(err.detail || "Login failed");
      }

      const data = await res.json();
      console.log("Login success:", data);
      // TODO: store token, redirect
    } catch (err: any) {
      setError(err.message || "Login failed");

      setLoading(false);
    }

Sebastian — perfect.

✅ FINAL app/login/page.tsx (copy & paste this EXACT file)
tsx


Copy
// app/login/page.tsx
"use client";

import { useState } from "react";

export default function LoginPage() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [password, setPassword] = useState("");
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);

  async function handleSubmit(e: React.FormEvent) {
    e.preventDefault();
    setLoading(true);
    setError(null);

    try {
      const res = await fetch("http://localhost:8000/auth/login", {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
        body: JSON.stringify({ email, password }),
      });

      if (!res.ok) {
        const err = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));
        throw new Error(err.detail || "Login failed");
      }

      const data = await res.json();
      console.log("Login success:", data);

      // TODO: store token, redirect user
      // Example:
      // localStorage.setItem("token", data.access_token);
      // window.location.href = "/";
    } catch (err: any) {
      setError(err.message || "Login failed");
    } finally {
      setLoading(false);
    }
  }

  return (
    <div className="flex items-center justify-center min-h-screen bg-slate-100">
      <div className="w-full max-w-sm bg-white p-8 rounded-xl shadow">
        <h1 className="text-2xl font-bold mb-6 text-center">Login</h1>

        <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="flex flex-col gap-4">
          <input
            type="email"
            placeholder="Email"
            className="p-3 border rounded text-sm"
            value={email}
            onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
            required
          />

          <input
            type="password"
            placeholder="Password"
            className="p-3 border rounded text-sm"
            value={password}
            onChange={(e) => setPassword(e.target.value)}
            required
          />

          {error && (
            <p className="text-sm text-red-600 text-center">{error}</p>
          )}

          <button
            type="submit"
            disabled={loading}
            className="p-3 bg-blue-600 text-white rounded text-sm hover:bg-blue-700 disabled:opacity-60"
          >
            {loading ? "Logging in..." : "Login"}
          </button>
        </form>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
🎯 What this version improves
✔ Full-page centered login
✔ Clean card UI
✔ Error handling
✔ Loading state
✔ Ready for token storage + redirect
✔ Works with your FastAPI backend (localhost:8000/auth/login)
